18 & 19 GEO . 5.-A.D. 1928 .
18 GEO . 5 .
ROYAL ASSENT , 29TH MARCH , 1928.
1.An Act to applycertainSums out ofthe ConsolidatedFund of
Northern Irelandto the serviceof the year ended on the thirty-
firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-seven,and of
the yearsending on the thirty-firstday of March, nineteen
hundred and twenty-eight, and the thirty-firstday of March,
nineteenhundred and twenty-nine. (ConsolidatedFund ).
2. An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts (Northern Ireland),
1922 to 1927,by extendingthe periodwithinwhich the Ministry
of Finance may give guaranteesunder the saidActs. (Loans
Guarantee .)
ROYAL ASSENT , 17th APRIL , 1928 ..
3. An Act to amend the Unemployment InsuranceActs (Northern
Ireland), 1920 to 1926. (Unemployment Insurance.)
18 & 19 GEO . 5 .
ROYAL ASSENT , 4TH JUNE , 1928 .
4. An Act to amend the provisionsofthe ConstabularyAct (Northern
Ireland), 1922, with respectto the distributionand the free
quotaoftheRoyal UlsterConstabulary;toenablecertainpay-
ments to be made towards the cost of the employment of the
saidConstabularyand the SpecialConstabularyin the county
borough ofBelfast;and otherwiseto amend thelaw with respect
to Constabularymatters. (Constabulary.)

(Legitimacy.)
6. An Act to amend the law relatingto perpetuitiesand accumula-
tions, as respectscertainbenefitfunds. [Superannuationand
otherTrust Funds (Validation).]
7. An Act to provide for and regulatethe payment of expenses
incurredby educationauthoritiesand committees in connection
with membership and meetings of educationassociations.
(Educations Associations.)

otherwise to make provisionsfor enabling certainleasesand
grants to be made for schoolpurposes. (SchoolSites.)
9. An Act to grant a duty of Excise upon certainlicences, and to
amend the law relatingto certainotherdutiesof Excise and to
stamp duty . (Finance .)
10. An Act to make furtherprovisionwith respectto the compulsory
acquisitionofland forroadsand streets,to conferfurtherpowers
upon localauthoritiesforthe improvement of roads and streets,
and forthe preventionof danger to personsusingthe same and
the reliefof congestionof traffic, and for other purposes con-
nected therewith. (Roads Improvement.)
11. An Act to provideforthe applicationto Northern Irelandof such
Act as may be passed in the presentsessionof the Parliament
of the United Kingdom for amending the National Health
InsuranceAct , 1924, and other enactments relatingto health
insurance, and otherwiseto amend the law relatingto health
insurance as respects Northern Ireland. (National Health
Insurance .)
12. An Act to apply a Sum out ofthe ConsolidatedFund ofNorthern
Irelandto the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-firstday
ofMarch,nineteenhundredand twenty-nine,and toappropriate
the Suppliesgrantedin thisSessionofParliament. (Appropria-
tion Act .)
13.An Act to amend theFisheries(Ireland)Acts, 1842 to 1921, to
provide for the regulationof the saleof salmon,troutand eels,
and tomake furtherprovisionforthepreservationofthefisheries
in Northern Ireland. (Fisheries.)
14. An Act to amend the enactments which relateto the making of
theappointmentsofOfficialArbitrators,theGovernment Chemist,
AuditorsofEducationalEndowments ,and Officersforthepur-
pose ofobtainingprobate or lettersof administrationin the case
of small estates. (AdministrativeProvisions.)
15.An Act to extend the duration of the CivilAuthorities(Special
Powers) Act (Northern Ireland), 1922. [Civil Authorities
(SpecialPowers).]

sixpence .

said ConsolidatedFund ,and apply towards making good

and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1.An insuredcontributorwho isunemployed shall,
ifhe proves that the statutoryconditionsare fulfilled
in his case and if he is not disqualifiedunder the
Unemployment InsuranceActs forthe receiptof benefit,
be entitled, subjectto the provisionsof those Acts, to
receive benefit .

as to

for receipt" 7.- (1) The statutory conditions for the
receiptof unemployment benefitby a person insured ofbenefit.under thisAct (inthisAct referredto as an insured
contributor ")are-
66
(i) That not lessthan thirty contributions
have been paid in respectof him as an
insuredcontributorin respectof the two
years immediately precedingthe date on
which applicationfor benefitis made ;
(ii) that he has made applicationforbenefit
in the prescribedmanner ,and provesthat
sincethe date of the applicationhe has
been continuouslyunemployed ;
(iii) that he iscapableof and availablefor
work ;
(iv) that he is genuinelyseekingwork but
unable to obtain suitableemployment ;
(v) that, if he has been required by an
insuranceofficer, in pursuance of regula-
tionsmade under thisAct by the Ministry
after consultationwith the Ministry of
Education, to attend at any course of
instructionapproved for the purposes of
this provision under the regulationsso
made , he proves that he duly attended
in accordance with the requirement ;
(vi) that he has, except as may be otherwise
prescribedby regulationsmade under this
Act ,been residentin the United Kingdom
for a period of three years immediately
preceding the date on which application
for benefit is made :
Provided that a person shallnot be deemed to
have failedto fulfilthe statutoryconditionsby reason
only that he has declined-
(a) an offer of employment in a situation
vacant in consequence of a stoppage of
work due to a trade dispute ; or

CHAPTER 5 .
An Act to amend the law relating to children born
out of wedlock . [4th June , 1928.]
BE and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) Subjectto the provisionsof thissection,
where the parents of an illegitimateperson marry or
have married one another, whether before or afterthe
commencement of this Act, the marriage shall, ifthe
fatherof the illegitimateperson was or isat the date of
the marriage domiciledin Northern Ireland,render that
person, ifliving, legitimatefrom the commencement of
thisAct , or from the date of the marriage, whichever
lasthappens .
(2) Nothing in thisAct shalloperateto legitimate
a person whose fatheror mother was married to a third
person when the illegitimateperson was born.
(3) The legitimationofa person under thisAct does
not enablehim or hisspouse,childrenor remoter issueto
take any interestin realor personalproperty save as is
hereinafterin thisAct expresslyprovided.
(4) The provisionscontainedin the Scheduleto this
Act shallhave effectwith respectto the re-registration
of the birthsof legitimatedpersons.
2.-(1) A person claimingthat he or hisparent or
any remoter ancestorbecame orhas become a legitimated
person may present a petition under the Legitimacy
DeclarationAct (Ireland), 1868, and that Act, subject
to such necessary modificationsas may be prescribed
by rules of court,shallapply accordingly.
(2) A petitionunder the saidAct may be presented
by any such person as aforesaidto the county court
insteadof to the High Court, and the county court on
such a petitionbeing presented shall have all such
jurisdictionas by the saidAct is conferredupon the
High Court :

Section 2
SCHEDULE .
REQUIREMENTS AS TO RULES OF REGISTERED FUNDS .
The rulesof a fund qualifiedforregistrationunder thisAct
must make provisionfor the followingmatters, that is to say :-
1. The whole of the objectsfor which the fund isestablished:
2. The appointment and removal of trusteesand of a secretary:
3. The vestingin the trusteesof allproperty belongingto the
fund :
4. The investment in the names of the trusteesof allcapital
moneys belongingto the fund and for authorisingthe
investments,ifany in additionto thoseauthorisedby law,
inwhich the trusteesmay investsuch moneys ;so,however ,
thatthe rulesof a fund may provideforthe depositof such
moneys with a bank ,and may alsoprovidefortheirdeposit
with the employers of personsemployed in the undertaking,
or combination of undertakings, in connectionwith which
thefund isestablished,inthe followingcases,thatisto say-
(a) where the rulesso providedbeforethetwenty-
ninth day of March , nineteen hundred and
twenty -eight ;
(b) where the depositof such moneys isauthorised
subjectto the conditionsthat every employer
with whom such moneys are depositedmust be
a body corporatehaving,during each of the ten
years lastpast beforethe date of any deposit,
paid a dividend or interestat a rate of not less
than threeper cent.on itsordinaryshares,and
that every such depositmust be secured by a
chargeon the whole or part of the assetsof the
undertaking carriedon by such employer.
5. The making of contributionsto the fund by the employer
of persons employed in the undertaking or combination
of undertakings in connection with which the fund is
established :

## Page 55

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] Superannuationand 45[Ch .6,7.]
otherTrust Funds (Validation) Act
(NorthernIreland),1928.
6.The contributionspayableto the fund, and the ratesof
benefitpayable thereoutor the method of calculating
thebenefitsso payable:
7.The conditionson which personsmay become and may
ceaseto be, respectively, contributorsto, and entitled
to benefitsfrom , the fund :
8.The circumstancesin which the fund may be wound up
and the manner in which the assetsthereof are in that event
to be applied:
9.The method by whichtherulesmay be amended :
10.The preparationof allstatementsof accounts, balance
sheetsand reportsrequiredby thisAct to be prepared:
11.The supplyon demand to every personhaving any rights
in the fund,beinga personwho isor has been employed
in the undertaking or combination of undertakings in
connectionwith which the fund is established, of a copy
of the rulesof the fund and of allamendments thereof,
and of the lateststatement of accounts,balancesheetand
report prepared in accordance with the requirements of
this Act .

prescribedunder this section.

21. This Act may be citedas the Roads Improve-
ment Act (Northern Ireland), 1928.
Short title.
SCHEDULE .
PRELIMINARY PROCEDURE .
1.The localauthority, where they proposeto acquireland
otherwisethan by agreement forthe purposeofimproving or widening
an old road or streetor making a new road or street,may submit to
theMinistryofHome Affairsan applicationinthe prescribedform
foran ordervestinginthelocalauthoritythelandspecifiedin the
application.
2. Notice of the applicationshallbe published by the local
authorityin the prescribedmanner , and such noticeshallbe given
both in the localityin which the land isproposed to be acquiredand
to the owners,lesseesand occupiersofthatland as may be prescribed.
Notice of theapplicationshallalsobe givento such Government
departmentsas may be prescribed.
3. On the expirationof one month afterthe publicationof the
noticeof the application,the Ministryof Home Affairs, aftercon-
sideringall objectionsto the applicationwhich may have been
presentedto the saidMinistryby personsinterestedin the land
specifiedintheapplication,and aftercausinga localinquiryto be held
(ifthe saidMinistrythinksitnecessaryto do so) as to the propriety
of making the order appliedfor,may make an order vestingin the
localauthoritythe saidland,or so much thereofas the saidMinistry
thinks proper.
Ifa localinquiryisheld as aforesaid,the localauthorityand all
personsinterestedin the land, and such other personsas the person
holding the inquiryin his discretionthinks fitto allow, shallbe
permittedto appearand to be heard at the inquiry,and beforemaking
the order,the MinistryofHome Affairsshallconsiderthe reportof the
personwho heldtheinquiry,and allobjectionsmade thereat.

## Page 87

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] Roads Improvement Act [Ch .10.] 77
(NorthernIreland),1928.
4. The order shallcontain such provisionsas the Ministryof
Home Affairsthinksnecessaryforthe purposeof carryingtheorder
intoeffect,and may provideforthesuspensionoftheoperationofthe
order,or any partthereof,untilthe localauthorityhave paid,or made
provisionto the satisfactionof the said Ministryforthe payment of,
compensationto personsinterestedin the land to which the order
relates,or in landinjuriouslyaffectedby the works proposedto be
carriedoutby thelocalauthority.
An ordermade by theMinistryofHome Affairsasaforesaidisin
this Schedule referred to as a vesting order."
5. A vestingorder,when made ,shallbe finaland have effectas
ifenactedinthisAct ;and themakingthereofby theMinistryofHome
Affairsshallbe conclusiveevidence that the requirements of this
Schedulehave been complied with,and that the orderhas been duly
made and iswithinthe powers of thisAct .
Noticeofthemaking of a vestingordershallbe publishedby
thelocalauthorityintheprescribedmanner,and shallalsobe given
tosuchpersonsand Government departments(includingtheMinistry
of Finance) as may be prescribed.
OPERATION OF VESTING ORDER .
6. A vestingordershallbe effectualto passand vestin the local
authority,asfrom suchdateas may be specifiedinthe vestingorder
(inthisSchedulereferredto as " thedate of vesting")an estatein
feesimpleinthelandto whichitrelates,dischargedfrom allclaims,
estates, incumbrancesor chargeswhatsoever; and the rightsand
claimsof allpersonsin respectof suchlandor any interesttherein
shall,as from thedateofvesting,be transferredand attached,tothe
extenttowhichcompensationmay be payableinaccordancewiththe
provisionsof thisSchedule, to the rateor fund out of which the
expensesof thelocalauthorityunderthisAct aredefrayed(inthis
Schedulereferredto as " the compensationfund"), and shallbe
dischargedby payments out of the compensationfund.
In so far as a vestingorder relatesto land, the ownership of
which isregisteredunder the LocalRegistrationof Title(Ireland)
Act,1891,thedateofvestingshall,notwithstandinganythinginthe
foregoingprovisionsof thisarticle, be eitherthe date specifiedin
the vestingorderas aforesaid, or the date of the lodgment of the
vestingorderwith the registeringauthorityunder the said Act,
whichever is the later .

relatestolandtheownershipofwhichisregisteredasaforesaid),shall,
forthwithupon productionofsuchvestingorder,be registeredinthe
properofficefortheregistrationofdeedsortitles,asthecaserequires.

remaining and contiguouslands and hereditaments,belongingto the

or interestcreatedafterthe saiddate in any land to which the vesting
orderrelates,shallany sum of money be awarded so as to increase
thetotalamountofcompensationwhichwouldotherwisehavebeen
requiredto be paid inrespectof the acquisitionof such lands.

by him of an award , correctany mistake therein, or supply any
accidentalomission therefrom .

CHAPTER 13 .
An Act to amend the Fisheries(Ireland)Acts,1842
to 1921 , to provide for the regulation of the sale
of salmon , trout and eels, and to make further
provisionforthe preservationof the fisheriesin
Northern Ireland . [4th June , 1928.]
B E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
PART I.
ELECTION AND MEMBERSHIP OF BOARDS OF
CONSERVATORS .
1.-(1) All conservatorsof fisheriesholding office
at the passing of thisAct shallcontinue in officeuntil
the seventh day of November , nineteen hundred and
thirty, when they shallcease to hold office, and new
boards of conservatorsshallbe electedpriorto that date
to hold officefrom that date .
A.D. 1928 ,
office ofTenureof
existingand
futureboards .
c . 88 .
(2) Sectionthirteenof the Fisheries(Ireland) Act , 13& 14Vict.,
1850, shallhave effectas iffor the words " threeyears
from the time of their elections " there were substituted
the words " fiveyearsfrom the seventhday of November
in the year in which theirelectionsare held.”
2. Any electedmember of a board of conservators
may at any time by noticein writingdeliveredto or
served by post upon the clerkof the board resignhis
membership of the board, whereupon the seatof such
member upon the board shallbecome vacant.

servators.

3.- (1) Whenever during the term of officeof any Fillingof
board of conservatorsthe seat of any electedmember
of the board becomes vacant by death, resignation, or
incapacity, it shall be lawful for the other members
of the board or such of them as shallbe present, by
resolutionduly passed at a meeting of the board,to
elect a person to be a member of the board during the
residueof the term of officeof the board in place of
the member whose seat isso vacant. Any vacancy so
arisingshallbe filledat or before the second meeting
of the board after the vacancy occurs.

(2) When the seatof any member of a board of

members of the board may , untilthe vacancy is filled
under this section, continue to act notwithstanding
such vacancy .
(3) Sectionten of the Fisheries(Ireland) Act,1850 ,
ishereby repealed.
PART II .
RESTRICTIONS ON SALE , & C., OF SALMON , TROUT AND
EELS .
4.-( 1) From and afterthe commencement of this
section,and save as otherwiseexpresslyprovided in this
Part of thisAct ,no person shallsell,expose for sale,or
keep for sale at any place, any salmon,trout, or eels
(otherthan salmon,trout,oreelsdried,or preservedin tins
or other containers or cooked and prepared for con-
sumptionat a meal)unlesshe isdulylicensedunder this
Part ofthisAct tosellsalmon,trout,or eelsat such place.
(2) An applicantfora licenceto sellsalmon,trout,
or eels shall make an applicationin writing in the
prescribedform to the clerkof the board ofconservators
of the districtin which the placewhere itisproposed to
sellis situated, and shallforward therewith a certificate
signed by a justiceof the peace that the said applicant
isa fitand proper person to receivesuch licence, and
the saidboard may thereupon issuethrough theirclerkto
such applicanta licencein the prescribedform to sell
salmon, trout, and eelsat such place, and may in like
manner from time to time renew,in the prescribedfo'm ,
any such licenceso issuedby them ,unlessthe same has
been terminated under this Part of this Act .
(3) When a board ofconservatorsrefusesto grant a
licenceor renewal of a licenceto sellsalmon,trout, or
eelsto an applicantwho has complied with the provisions
of the foregoingsub-section,the applicantmay appeal in
the prescribedform to the MinistryofCommerce ,and the
said Ministryshallthereupon give to the said board of
conservatorsfourteencleardays'noticein writingof the
said Ministry'sintentionto consider the said appeal,
and aftertaking into considerationany representations
which the saidboard may make beforethe expirationof
suchnotice,thesaidMinistrymay ,ifitdeems itexpedient
to do so, grant to the applicanta licenceor renewal of a

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] 97Fisheries Act [Ch .13.]
(NorthernIreland),1928.
licence,which shallhave the same effectas ifithad been
granted by the saidboard.
(4) A fee of fiveshillingsshallbe payable by the
licenceholder in respectof each such licenceor renewal
oflicencetothe board ofconservatorsby whom thelicence
or renewal of licenceis granted, and a separateand
distinctlicenceshallbe taken out by every personpropos-
ing tosellsalmon, trout, or eelsin respectof each
separateand distinctplaceor setof premiseswhere itis
proposed to sellthe same .
(5) Every suchlicenceshallbe terminatedby-
(a) the death of the holder;or
(b) revocationby the Ministry of Commerce
under thisPart of thisAct ; or
(c) surrenderby the holder.
(6) Every such licenceand every renewal thereof
shall(unlessthelicenceispreviouslyterminated)continue
in forceuntilthe expirationofthe calendaryear inwhich
the licencewas granted or lastrenewed,as the case may
be, and shallthen expire.
(7) If the holder of a licenceto sellsalmon ,trout,
or eels is convicted of an offence under the Fisheries
Acts or thisAct ,the Ministryof Commerce may revokesuch licence: Provided thatthe said Ministryshallgive
to the holder of the licence and the board of conservators
by whom the licencewas issuedfourteencleardays'
notice of the intentionto revoke the licence, and shall
consider any representationswhich the holder or the
board may make to the said Ministrybefore the
expirationof such notice.

not duly licensed; or

this Part of this Act ; or
(c) buys any salmon,trout,or eelsfrom any person
(otherthan a persontowhom therequirements
ofthisPart ofthisAct with respectto licences
do not apply)who isnot duly licensedto sell

PART III .
LICENCE DUTIES .
11.-(1) The FisheriesActs shallbe construed and
have effect as if for the several licence duties numbered
1, 4, and 6, in the Scheduleto the Fisheries(Ireland)
Act, 1848,as amended by the Salmon Fishery(Ireland)
Act ,1863,and the Salmon and Freshwater FisheriesAct ,
1921,therewere substitutedthe licencedutiesfollowing,

(3) If any board of conservators so determine
and resolve, a licencefor angling with a singlesalmon
rod in theirdistrictduring the limitedperiodof fourteen
days from the date of the licencemay be issuedon pay-
ment of the licenceduty of one pound .
12. The powers conferredupon boards of conserv-
ators by sectiontwenty -one of the Fisheries(Ireland)
Act , 1848,to fixthe licenceduty payable on any engine,
instrument,net,weir,or deviceto which the saidsection
applies,shallbe transferredto the MinistryofCommerce ,
and that Ministrymay exercisethosepowers withoutany
applicationbeingmade to itby anyone in thatbehalf,
and references in the said section to boards of con-
servatorsshallbe construed, so far as applicable, as
references to the said Ministry.
PART IV .
ADMINISTRATION AND LEGAL PROCEEDINGS .

the powers conferredby thissection, and every officer

that isto say :-

believedto be conveying fishof any kind, or
any instrument, poison or explosiveused or
adapted fortaking fishillegally,and to inspect
any fishand any such instrument which such

shallas soon as convenientlymay be take such stepsas

been committed ,in relationto such fishor other article
dealt with accordingto law.
(3) Where any person detainsin hiscustody under
the authorityof thissectionany fish, and such fishis
likelyto become unfitforhuman food beforethe matter
can convenientlybe dealtwith by any court,such person
shallproduce such fishto a justiceof the peace, and ,
ifauthorisedso to do by such justiceof the peace,shall
destroy such fish.
(4) A justiceof the peace to whom any fishis
produced in pursuance of this sectionshall, if he is
of opinion that the fishought in the circumstancesto
be destroyed, give to the person producing the fisha
certificatein writingdescribingthe fishand any marks ,
peculiarities, or other particularsthereof pointed out
to him by such person, and authorisingsuch person to
destroy the fish; and such certificateshallbe conclusive
evidence in every court of allsuch matters of fact as
aforesaid as are stated therein .
(5) No person shallbe liableforany lossor damage
occasionedby or in the course of the exerciseof any of
thepowersconferredon him by thissection,unlesssuch
lossor damage was causedby such personwantonly or
maliciously.

CHAPTER 17 .
An Act to provide forthe maintenance of proper
standards of quality in connection with the
marketing of potatoes in certaincases,and for
the licensing of persons engaged in such
marketing ; and for other purposes connected
therewith . [18th December , 1928.]
B
E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of Nor-
thern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled, and
by the authorityof the same ,as follows:--
1. Except as otherwise provided by this Act , a
person shallnot send or attempt to send potatoesfrom
Northern Irelandto Great Britain, the IrishFree State
or the Isleof Man , unless he holds a licencefor that
purpose under thisAct .
2.-(1) Subjectto the provisionsof thisAct, the
Ministry ofAgricultureshallhave power to grant,revoke
and suspend licencesauthorisingthe persons named
thereinto send potatoesfrom Northern Irelandto Great
Britain,the IrishFree Stateand the IsleofMan .
(2) The Ministryof Agricultureshall, on appli-
cation being made in the prescribedmanner , and on
payment of the feespecifiedin thissection,grant to any
person, upon such conditionsas may be prescribed, a
licencefor the purposes aforesaid:
Provided that the said Ministry may revoke or
suspend a licenceif satisfiedthat the holder thereof
has not complied with the prescribedconditions, and
may refuseto grant a licenceto an applicantwho was
formerly licensedunder thisAct , but whose licencehas
been revoked .
(3) A licencegrantedunder thissectionshallbe
in the prescribedform , and shallremain in forceuntil
revokedor suspendedby the MinistryofAgricultureby
reason of the non -compliance of the holderof the licence

Act , 1888 . [18th December , 1928.]
BE itenactedE itenactedby the King'smost ExcellentMajesty,
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1.-(1) The Borough Funds (Ireland) Act, 1888
(in thisAct referredto as " the principalAct ") shall
have effectas iffor sectionseven of that Act (which

## Page 141

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] Borough Funds Act 131[Ch .22.]
(NorthernIreland),1928.
relatesto the vote of the electorsof a district)therewere
substitutedthe followingsection:-
" 7. No expense in relationto the promotion
of a Bill in Parliament shall be charged by the
governing body of a districtunder this Act unless
the requirementscontained in the Schedule to this
Act have been observed ."
(2) The principalAct shallhave effectas if for
the Schedules to the said Act there were substituted the
Schedule to this Act .
(3) Ifthe resultof a pollunder the principalAct
as amended by thisAct,or the decision,when final,of a
meeting of localgovernment electorsof the district(in
thisAct referredto as " electors"), is againstthe pro-
motion ofthe Bill,orofa partorpartsorclauseorclauses
of the Bill, the governing body shallforthwith take all
necessarystepsto withdraw the Bill,or the part or parts
or clause or clauses(as the case may be) againstwhich
the pollhas resultedor the decisionof the meeting has
been given.
In the case of equalityof votes on any question
ofpromotion,that questionshallbe deemed to be decided
against the promotion.
(4) Where a Bill, or a part or parts or clauseor
clausesofa Bill,isor arewithdrawn,no furtherexpense
shallbe incurredby the governingbody or mayor or
chairman in or about the promotion of the Bill, or part
or partsor clauseor clauses,so withdrawn ; but,subject
as aforesaid, all costs, charges and expenses incurred
by the governing body or mayor or chairman in, or as
incidentalto,the preparationand promotion of the Bill
up to and inclusiveof itsdepositin Parliamentand
withdrawal (when withdrawn ), and in, or as incidental
to,the holdingof a meeting or the takingof a pollunder
the principalAct as amended by thisAct , shall, when

SCHEDULE .
PART I.
REGULATIONS FOR MEETING OF ELECTORS .
1.Where the governingbody of a districthave resolved, in
accordancewith the provisionsofthisAct, to promote a BillinParlia-
ment ,and the Billhas been deposited,noticeshallbe givenby placards
and by advertisement in some localnewspaper circulatingin the
districtin two successiveweeks stating-
(a) the titleof the Bill;and
(6) a briefstatementofthe objectsof theBill; and
(c) thattheBillhas beendeposited,and thedateon which it
was firstdeposited,in Parliament;and
(d) thatcopiesoftheBillmay be inspectedand purchasedat
a placewithin the districtspecifiedin the notice,between
the hours of ten in the forenoon and half-past four in the
afternoon,on every week day fortwenty-one days afterthe
date of the firstadvertisement, and that extractsmay be
taken freeof charge ; and
(e) that a publicmeeting of electorswillbe held at a specified
place on a day named ,not being lessthan twenty-one nor
more than twenty-eightdays afterthe firstadvertisement
of the notice, for the purpose of consideringthe question
of the promotion of the Bill, and indicatingthe resolutions
which willbe submitted to the meeting.
2. The firstadvertisementunder theseregulationsmust be made
withinsevendaysfromthefirstdepositoftheBillinParliament,and
the placardsgivingnoticeunder theseregulationsmust be posted
within the same time .

PART II .
REGULATIONS FOR TAKING A POLL .
1. The presidingofficerforthe purpose of takinga pollshallbe
themayor or chairmanof thegoverningbody of thedistrict,or,in
the event of the mayor or chairman being unable or unwillingto act
as presidingofficer,thepresidentofthemeetingin respectofwhich
thepollwas required,and allpowersanddutiesby thisSchedulevested
in or imposedon the presidingofficer,and allotherdutiesrequired
to be performedby him in relationto the takingof a poll,shallbe
exercisedand performedby such mayor, chairman or presidentas
aforesaid .
2. Iftheofficeofmayor or chairmanofthegoverningbody is
vacant at the time when any such power or duty must be exercised
orperformed,orifthemayor orchairmanofthegoverningbody,or
the presidentof the saidmeeting,as the casemay be,isunable,from
illnessorothersufficientcause,toexerciseorperformsuchpowers or
duties, or is absent or refusesto act, some other person shallbe
appointedby the governingbody to exerciseor perform such powers
and duties .
3. The governingbody shall,beforeor during the poll,appoint
a competentnumber ofpersonsto assistthepresidingofficerincon-
ducting and completing the same .

CHAPTER 26 .
An Act to provide forthe establishment,mainten-
ance and management of a fund forthe payment
of compensation to the owners of certain live
stock,which are exported from Northern Ireland
and slaughtered under the authority of law at a
port in Great Britain in consequence of an
outbreak,or suspected outbreak or apprehended
danger ,of foot and mouth disease ; and to make
provision for the method of investigating and
determining claims forsuch compensation .
B
[18th December ,1928
E itenactedby the King'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:---
1.-(1) For the purposes of thisAct thereshallbeestablisheda body (in this Act referredto as " the
Trustees"),which shallbe a body corporateby the name
ofthe SlaughteredAnimals (Compensation)Trusteesfor
Northern Ireland, with perpetualsuccessionand a com-
mon seal .
(2) The sealof the Trusteesshallbe authenticated
by the signatureof any one of the Trustees, or of the
secretaryto the Trusteesduly authorisedby them to act
in thatbehalf,and any document purportingto be sealed
with the seal so authenticated shall be received as
evidence of the particularsstatedin that document .
2.-(1) The Trustees shallconsistof six persons,
appointmentallof whom shallbe appointedas occasionrequiresby
and
constitution
of Trustees .
such organisation, consistingof representativesof the
bodies now known as " The North of Ireland Cattle
Traders ' and Stock Owners ' Association " and " The
Londonderry and North -West Cattle Dealers' and
Shippers'Association," as may be formed by thosebodies
and recognisedby the Ministry of Agriculturefor the
purposesof thisAct ; and such organisationas aforesaid
is in this Act referred to as " the Association ."

## Page 167

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] SlaughteredAnimals 157[Ch . 26.]
(Compensation) Act.
(Northern Ireland), 1928.
(2) Every appointment made by the Association
as aforesaidshallbe evidencedby writingunder the
hand of the chairman of the Association .
(3) Such member of the Trustees as the Trustees
shallfrom time to time nominate forthe purposeshall
be the chairman of the Trustees .
(4) The Trusteesshallappoint a fitand proper
person (not being a member of the Trustees)to be their
secretary, and there shallbe paid to such secretaryout
of the funds at the disposalof the Trusteesunder this
Act such remuneration, not exceeding the sum of one
hundred pounds per annum ,and expenses (ifany )as the
Trusteesmay from time to time determine.
(5) The provisionscontained in the Schedule to
thisAct shallhave effectwith respectto the term of
office,meetings and procedure of the Trustees.
(6) The firstappointment of Trustees shall be
made on orbeforesuch date as the MinistryofAgriculture
may determine.
3.-( 1) Every member of the Trustees shallbe a
person who is ordinarilyresidentin Northern Ireland
and is engaged in the businessof exporting livestock
from Northern Ireland .
(2) At leastfour members of the Trustees shall
be personsengaged in the businessof exportingcattle
or sheep from Northern Ireland,and at leastone member
of the Trustees shall be a person engaged in the
businessof exportingpigsfrom Northern Ireland.
4.-(1) The Trusteesshallestablish,maintainand
manage inaccordancewith thisAct a fund to be known as
the Slaughtered Animals (Compensation ) Fund for
Northern Ireland(in thisAct referredto as " the com-
pensationfund ").
(2) There shallbe creditedto the compensation

SCHEDULE .
TERM OF OFFICE , MEETINGS AND PROCEDURE OF THE TRUSTEES .
Term of Office.
1. Subject to the provisionsof article2 of thisSchedule,every
member ofthe Trusteesshall,unlesshe soonerdies,resigns,or becomes
disqualified,hold hisofficeas such member forthe term of ten years to
be reckoned-
(a) inthecaseofthefirstmembers,from thefirstappointment
of the Trustees ;and
(b) in thecaseofevery subsequentmember ,from theexpiration
of the term of officeof his predecessor.
2. A member ofthe Trusteesappointedto filla casualvacancy in
the membership of the Trusteesshall,unlesshe soonerdies,resignsor
becomes disqualified,holdofficefortheresidueoftheterm forwhich the
member ,whose death,resignationor disqualificationoccasionedthe
vacancy,would haveheldofficeifhe had notdied,resignedorbecome
disqualified.
3. A member of the Trusteesmay at any time resignhis office
as such member by letteraddressedto the secretaryof the Trustees,
and every such resignationshalltake effectat the commencement of
the meeting of the Trusteescommencing next afterthe receiptof such
resignationby the Trustees.
4. A member of the Trusteesshallbecome disqualifiedfor office
as such member upon the happening of any of the followingevents,
that is to say :-
(a) The absenceof suchmember from fourconsecutiveordinary
meetings of the Trustees;
(b) The ceasing of such member to have the qualifications
requiredby thisAct formembership of the Trustees.
5. Every member of the Trusteesshall,on the cessationof his
membership by lapseoftime,be eligibleforre-appointment.
Meetings of the Trustees.
6. The firstordinarymeeting of the Trusteesshallbe held not
laterthan one month afterthe appointment of the firstmembers of
the Trustees; and allsubsequent ordinarymeetings of the Trustees
shallbe heldat suchtimes(not beinglessfrequentlythan once in every
period of three consecutivemonths ) as the Trustees may appoint
eithergenerallyor in respectof any particularordinarymeeting .
7.- (i) The firstmeeting of the Trustees for the purpose of
appointinga Chairman ,and transactingany othernecessarybusiness
ofa preliminarynature,shallbe summoned by theMinisterofAgricul-
ture for Northern Ireland .
(ii) The firstordinarymeeting ofthe Trusteesshallbe summoned
by the Chairman of the Trusteesby noticesentby post addressed to
each member ofthe Trusteesat hisusualplaceofresidence,and every
subsequent ordinarymeeting of the Trusteesshallbe summoned by
theirsecretaryin the prescribedmanner .

occupationare, by virtueof the provisionsof
sub-section(3) of the lastforegoingsection,
treated as if they formed parts of a single
hereditament, each of the several heredita-
ments shallbe deemed to be occupiedand used
forindustrialpurposesand forotherpurposes
respectivelyinthe proportionin which, ifall
the hereditaments formed a singleheredita-
ment , that single hereditament would be
deemed to be so occupiedand used.

7.-(1) Inthevaluationlistseveryfreight-transport
hereditament which is occupied and used wholly for
transportpurposesshallbe shown as beingso occupied freight-
and used, and as respects every such hereditament heredita-
occupiedand used partlyfortransportpurposesthe net ments.
annual valuethereofshallbe apportionedby the Com-

occupationand userthereofforotherpurposes.
(2) Where a freight-transporthereditament isnot
occupied and used for more than one transportpurpose
the nature of that purpose shallbe shown , and where a
freight-transport hereditament is occupied and used
partlyforone transportpurposeand partlyforeither
orboth ofthe othertransportpurposes,the proportions
of the net annual value of the hereditament attributable
to the occupation and user thereof for the several trans-
port purposes shallbe distinguished.

portionsa freight-transporthereditamentisoccupiedand

SCHEDULE .
PROVISIONS FOR BRINGING INTO CONFORMITY WITH THIS ACT VALUATION
LISTSWHICH WILL BE IN FORCE ON THE IST DAY OF OCTOBER ,1929.
1. As soon as may be afterthe passingof thisAct the secretary
of every county counciland the clerkof every urban districtcouncil
shallpublisha noticein the prescribedform ofthe passingof thisAct ,
containing-
(a) a directionthat the occupierof any hereditament,who
claims that his hereditament is an industrialhereditament
or a freight-transporthereditament withinthe meaning of
thisAct ,shall,within thirtydays afterthe publicationof
the noticesend to such secretaryor clerk,as the case may
require, a claim in the prescribedform containing the
prescribedparticulars;
(b) a statement of the placeswhere forms of claim may be
obtained .
2.Within fourteendays aftertheexpirationofthesaidperiod
of thirtydays the secretaryof the county councilor clerkof the urban
districtcouncil,as thecasemay require(inthisSchedulereferredto
as" thesecretaryor clerk") shallmake out a fulland completelist

CHAPTER i.
An Act to empower the Lord Mayor Aldermen
and Citizens of the City of Belfast to alienate
lands for Hospital purposes ; and for other
purposes . [4th June , 1928.]
W HEREAS the City of Belfast(in thisAct called A.D.1928.
" the City") isa county borough subjectto the
Acts relatingto Municipal Corporations in Northern
Ireland and the Lord Mayor Aldermen and Citizensof
the City (in thisAct called" the Corporation" ) acting
by the Councilarethe urban sanitaryauthorityforthe
district thereof :
And whereas itis expedient that the Corporation
shouldbe empowered toalienatecertainlandsintheCity
for Hospital purposes:
And whereas it is expedient that the other pro-
visions in this Act contained should be enacted :
And whereas the objects aforesaid cannot be
attainedwithout the authorityof Parliament :
And whereas in relationto the promotion of the
BillforthisAct the requirementsof the Borough Funds
(Ireland)Act 1888 have been observed :
MAY IT THEREFORE PLEASE YOUR MAJESTY
That it may BE ENACTED AND BE IT ENACTED

of Commons of Northern Irelandin thispresentParlia-

1. This Act may be citedas the BelfastCorporation Shorttitle.

CHAPTER ii.

Dromore , County Down , to extend their

£ 15,000 over and above and in addition to
the borrowing powers conferred upon Urban
DistrictCouncils by Section 238 (2) of the
Public Health (Ireland) Act , 1878 .
[4th June , 1928.]
WHEREAS the Urban District of Dromore in the
County ofDown NorthernIrelandisan Urban District
withinthe meaning of the LocalGovernment (Ireland)
Act ,1898,61 & 62 Vic.Cap .37 and isunder the manage-
ment and control of the Urban District Council of Dromore
which Districtand Council are in thisAct respectively
referred to as " the District " and " the Council " and the
Councilisalsothe Urban SanitaryAuthority within the
meaning ofthe PublicHealth (Ireland),Act 1878.
And whereas itis expedient to make further and
better provisionsin regard to (a) Public Water Supply
for the District; (b) Sewerage Scheme for the District;
(c)Improvement of the roads and streetsin the District;
and (d)Generallyin relationto the Health Local Govern-
ment and improvement of the District.
And whereas the objects aforesaid cannot be
attained without having firstobtained the authority
of Parliament to extend the Borrowing Powers of the
Council .
And whereas in relationto the promotion of the
BillforthisAct the requirementsof the Borough Funds
51& 82Vist., (Ireland) Act , 1888,have been observed.с .53 .
And whereasby virtueoftheprovisionsofSection
41&42Viet., 238 of The Public Health (Ireland) Act , 1878, the
borrowing powers of the Council are limitedto the sum
of £ 11,459 18s. Od .
c .52 .
And whereas the Councilhave borrowed pursuant
to the powers them thereunto enabling the sum of
£2,188 7s. 3d., leaving unexpended a balance of
£9,271 10s. 9d.as on the 30th September , 1927.

CHAPTER v.
An Act togive statutoryeffectto the Constitution
of the ReligiousBody known as the Methodist
Church in Ireland and to provide for the altera-
tion and amendment of same , to confer
additional powers upon the Annual Conference

Preamble .
(NorthernIreland),1928.
WHEREAS inor about theyear 1739 John Wesley ,
lateof LincolnCollege, Oxford, Clerkin Holy Orders,
foundeda religiousSociety,ofwhich themembers subse-
quentlybecame generallyknown by thename ofMetho-
distsor Wesleyan Methodists,which Societywas intro-
duced intoIrelandinthe year 1747 ;
And whereas diversbuildingsin Great Britainand
Ireland commonly calledChapels, with a messuage or
dwellinghouseschool-houses or otherappurtenances were
from time to time given or conveyed by the said John
Wesley and other persons to Trustees upon trust(inter
alia) to permit and suffersuch person and persons and
for such time and times as should be appointed by the
Yearly Conference of the people called Methodists in
London , Bristol or Leeds, and no others to have and
enjoy the said premises for the purposes of preaching
and expoundingGod's Holy Word ;
And whereas for the purpose of renderingeffectual
the trustscreatedby the said severalgiftsand convey-
ances,and that no doubt or litigationmight arisewith
respectto the same ,or the interpretationor truemeaning
thereof, the said John Wesley executed a Deed Poll of
Declarationdated the 28th day ofFebruary,1784,which
saidDeed was duly enrolledinthe High Court ofChancery
inEngland ;
aAnd whereas the said Deed Poll contained
Declarationby the said John Wesley that the Yearly
Conference of the people calledMethodists had always
theretoforeconsistedof the preachers and expounders
of God's Holy Word , commonly called Methodist
Preachers in connection with and under the care of the
said John Wesley whom he had thought expedient to
summon to meet him in London ,Bristolor Leeds to advise
with them for the promotion of the Gospel of Christto
appoint the personso summoned and the otherpreachers
and expounders of God's Holy Word ,alsoin connection
with and under the care of the said John Wesley , not
summoned to the said Yearly Conference, to the use
and enjoyment ofthesaidChapelsand premisesso con-
veyed upon trustas aforesaid, and forthe expulsionof
unworthy and admissionof new personsunder hiscare
and intohis connectionto be preachersand expounders
as aforesaidand alsoof other persons upon trialfor the

Church in Irelandhas been duly enrolled;
And whereas divers buildings, Chapels, Schools,
Halls, messuages and dwellinghousesin variousparts of
Ireland are now held by trusteesupon various trusts
for the use of such Preachers in connection with the
Methodist Church in Ireland, as the Legal Conference
should from time to time appoint ;
And whereas by reason of the contemplated amal-
gamationoftheWesleyan Methodistand otherChurches
in England the Legal Conference may shortlycease to
exist ;
And whereas it is expedient that allpowers and
authoritiesvested in and exercisableby the Legal Con-
ferencein respectof the MethodistChurch in Ireland
should henceforthbe vested in and exercisableby the
Conference of the Methodist Church in Ireland :
And whereas under the eleventh Clause of the Deed
Poll it is provided that no person except ordained
Ministersof the Church of England may be appointed
for more than three years successivelyto the use and
enjoyment of any Chapel, and itisexpedientthatsuch
limitationsof appointment should be alteredas herein-
after provided ;

STATUTORY TRUSTS .
Upon Trustthatalland singularthe landsand premisestogether
withallbuildings(ifany)erectedortobeerectedthereonshallbeused
and occupied according to the nature thereoffor allor any of the
purposes hereaftermentioned that isto say :-
(a) As a Church Chapel or House of Worship or as a sitefora
Church Chapel or House of Worship,forthe use and benefit
of the Methodist Church in Ireland to the intent that the
Church and the severalmembers thereofmay thereinhave
God's Holy Word preachedand expounded and allother
Christianacts and ceremonies done and performed and
meetings heldinaccordancewith the usage of the Methodist
Church in Ireland .
(b) As a Schoolroom or Schoolhouse,orasa sitefora Schoolroom
or Schoolhouse,to the intentthat the Church may have a
Schoolor Schoolsor Sunday Schoolconducted in such
Schoolroom or Schoolhouse in accordance with Resolutions
from time to time passed by the Conference and either
subjecttotheexclusivecontroloftheConference,orsubject
to theRulesand RegulationsoftheMinistryofEducation,
as the Conferenceshallby resolutiondecide.
(c) As a Minister'sresidence,orasa sitefora Minister'sresidence,
to the intentthat the same may be used and occupied as a
residenceby the Ministeror Ministersappointed to the
Circuitfor the time being wherein such premises shallbe
situateor by such Supernumerary Ministeror Ministeron
Probation as may be permittedby the Conferenceto reside
therein rent free .
(d) As an Orphanage Almshouse Institutionor Hall forCharit-
ableor religiouspurposes,or as a sitetherefor,to the intent
that the same may be used and occupiedfor the use and
benefitof the Church and any Charitablepurpose in con-
nection therewith .
(e) As a Burial ground for the interment of members of the
Church and such otherpersonsastheConferencemay permit
to be buried therein in accordance with such Rules and
Regulationsas the Conferencemay make or approve.

CHAPTER vi.
An Act to separate and transferthe Theological
Endowments of the Methodist College,Belfast;
to incorporate the Governing Bodies of the
Methodist College,Belfast,and of the Edgehill
Theological College,Belfast; to provide for the
management and administration of the said
respectiveColleges, and the Endowments thereof
respectively, and for other purposes .
[4th June , 1928.]
WHEREAS by Indenture (hereinaftercalled the
Trust Deed ) dated the 24th day of August , 1865, the
lands and premisessetout in Schedule A Part 1 hereto
were acquiredby Trusteesforthe purposeof erecting
thereon a Collegeto be called" The Wesleyan Methodist
CollegiateInstitution" and to be used, along with the
rentsissuesand profitsthereof, for the use benefitand
advantage of the Society of People called Wesleyan

## Page 293

[18 & 19 GEO . 5.] MethodistCollegeAct 283[Ch . vi.]
(Northern Ireland), 1928.
Methodists (hereinaftercalledthe Methodist Church in
Ireland) and othersfor the purposesthereinspecified,
and with and subjectto the provisoesthereincontained.
And whereas,intheyear 1865,a Collegewas founded
under thename of " The Wesleyan MethodistCollegiateInstitution" (now known as the Methodist College,
Belfast) and was erectedand establishedupon the said
lands and premises, and has since been maintained
extended and improved, by means of funds chiefly
contributed as voluntary benefactionsby members of
the Methodist Church and by funds provided and set
apart by the " Yearly Conference" or Governing Body
of the Methodist Church in Irelandfor the purposes of
the College.
And whereas since the foundation of the College
certainmoneys ,funds,securities,and propertyhave been
contributed, acquired or accumulated, and certainbe-
quests have been made for certainspecialeducational
purposes connected with the said College, and amongst
other purposesforthe educationand trainingofDivinity
Students being Candidates for the Ministry of the
Methodist Church, and for the education and benefitof
the sons and daughters of Methodist Ministers.
And whereas from time to time certain additional
property,realand personal,has been acquiredforallor
some ofthe purposesofthe saidCollegeby the Governing
Body thereoffor the time being.
And whereas intheyear 1888 a Scheme was adopted
under the provisionsof the Educational Endowments
(Ireland)Act,1885,(hereinaftercalled" the1885Act ")
for the government management and control of the
College and its Endowments .
And whereas the said Scheme was pursuant to the
terms thereofand under the provisionsof the said.1885
Act alteredand amended in the year 1908 ;and again in
the year 1919.
And whereas by the Methodist Church in Ireland
Act,1915,a Body Corporatewas createdwithperpetual
succession and a Common Seal under the name of " The
Trustees of the Methodist Church in Ireland," with
power tohold and receivelands,money or otherproperty,
given, conveyed or otherwiseassuredto them, to be

66
The Conferenceconsidersitexpedientto separate

followingfurtherResolution:-

TheologicalDepartment from the Methodist
College,approvesoftheseveralrecommendations

upon thegenerallineslaiddown intheReport."

43.-(1) The PrincipaloftheEdgehillCollegeshall
be a Ministerin connectionwith the Methodist Church
in Ireland. His remuneration and allowances, and the
conditionsof his appointment shallbe determined from
time to time by the EdgehillGovernors. The appoint-
ment of the Principalshallbe made by the Conference.
He shallhold his officeforthe term of one year,and his
appointment or re-appointment shallbe made by the
Conference in accordance with itsrulesand regulations
forsuchappointments. ShouldthePrincipaldie,resign,
be suspended or dismissedduring the courseof the year,
the Edgehill Governors shall, if they think proper,
nominate to the President of the Methodist Church in
Ireland some other fit, proper and qualifiedperson for
appointment to act in his stead untilthe ensuing Con-
ference. If and whenever any Principalof the Edgehill
Collegeshallceaseto be a Ministerin connectionwith the
Methodist Church he shallthereupon vacatehisofficeand
a vacancy shallthereupon be consideredto have occurred
in such officein the same manner as ifthe Principalhad
then died .
(2) Any Tutor who shall be a Minister of the
Methodist Church shallbe appointed and re-appointed
in likemanner and subjectto the same conditionsas the
Principal. :

certified, and thereupon the same and allsecuritiesand

Short title .
ProvisionalOrder Confirmation
(Dromore Waterworks) Act
(NorthernIreland),1928.
CHAPTER vii.
An Act to confirm a Provisional Order of the
Ministry of Home Affairsrelatingto the Urban
District of Dromore . [4th June , 1928. ]
W HEREAStheMinistryofHomeAffairshasmade
the Provisional Order set out in the schedule
hereto under the provisions of the Public Health
(Ireland)Act , 1878 :
And whereas it is requisitethat the said Order
should be confirmed by Parliament :
Be itthereforeenactedby the King'smost Excellent
Majesty,and the Senateand the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthesame ,asfollows:-
1. The Order set out in the schedule hereto shall be
and the same ishereby confirmed and allthe provisions
thereofshallhave fullvalidityand force.
2. This Act may be citedas the Ministryof Home
AffairsProvisionalOrder Confirmation(Dromore Water-
works)Act (Northern Ireland), 1928.
SCHEDULE .
URBAN DISTRICT OF DROMORE .
ProvisionalOrder to enable the Council of the Urban
Districtof Dromore to put in forcethe compulsory
clausesoftheLands ClausesActs.
Dromore
Waterworks
Order .
41 & 42
Vict , c .52 .
WHEREAS theCouncilofthe Urban DistrictofDromore (inthisOrder
referredto as " the districtcouncil") requiretopurchaseand take the
landswater and rightsdescribedinthe Scheduleheretoforthe purpose
ofprovidinga supplyofwaterforthesaidUrban District:
Now thereforethe MinistryofHome AffairsforNorthern Ireland
inpursuanceofthe powers vestedinitby sectiontwo hundred and three
ofthePublicHealth(Ireland)Act,1878,andofallotherpowersenabling

## Page 327

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] MinistryofHome Affairs [Ch.vii.] 317
ProvisionalOrder Confirmation
(Dromore Waterworks) Act
(NorthernIreland),1928.
thesaidMinistryinthatbehalfherebyordersthatfrom and afterthe A.D.1928.
date of the Act of ParliamentconfirmingthisOrder the following
provisionsshallhave effect,thatistosay:-
1. The districtcouncilshallbe empowered to put in forcewith
referenceto the landswaterand rightsdescribedinthe Schedulehereto
the powers ofthe Lands ClausesActsasamended by sectioneightofthe
PublicHealth(Ireland)Act,1896,and modifiedby theAcquisitionof
Land (Assessmentof Compensation) Act, 1919,with respectto the
purchase and taking of lands otherwisethan by agreement or any of
them .
2. For the purposeofthisOrdertheexpression" land" in the
Lands ClausesActsshallincludethelandswaterand rightsdescribed
in the Schedule hereto .

CHAPTER viii.
Preamble .
An Act forincorporatingand conferringpowers on
the Antrim ElectricitySupply Company and
for other purposes . [18th December ,1928].
WHEREAS the supplyof electricitywithinthe
area definedby thisAct would be of publicand local
benefit .
And whereas the provisionof such supply would
be facilitatedby the constructionof works (as by this
Act authorised) for enablingelectricityto be generated

## Page 329

[18 & 19 GEO .5.] Antrim ElectricitySupply Act [Ch .viii.] 319
(NorthernIreland),1928.
at the generatingstationin thisAct describedby means
of hydraulic power derivedfrom the waters of the River
Bann and its tributariesand from Lough Beg and
Lough Neagh .
And whereas the persons in thisAct named with
others are willingat theirown expense to undertake the
constructionof such generatingstationand works and
the provisionof such supply of electricityand it is
expedient that they be incorporated into a Company
(hereinaftercalled" the Company " ) and that powers
be conferred on them for the purposes aforesaidand
generallyforcarryingout the objectsand provisionsof
this Act .
And whereas it is expedient that provisionsbe
enacted for enablingthe Company and localauthorities
companies and other persons to make contracts and
agreementsforthe supplyofelectricityinbulkor other-
wise and for other purposes .
And whereas the maintenance of the Lower Bann
as a navigableriverforthepurposesofthrough navigation
past Carnroe Weir would prevent the most economical
user of the waters of that River for the generationof
Electricityand itwould be in the publicinterestfor the
proper functioningofthe works as by thisAct authorised
to interruptthe through navigationof the River Bann
at Carnroe Weir and to modify orrepealtherights,powers
and obligationsof the Lower Bann Navigation Trustees
and ofotherbodiesor personsifany having rightspowers
and obligationsin connectionwith the navigationof the
saidRiver in so faras through navigationisconcerned.
And whereas the Belfast and North East Ireland
Electricityand Power Gas Company have not com-
menced theirworks forthe purpose of carryingout their
powers under the Belfastand North East IrelandElec-
tricityand Power Gas Act 1904 and itisexpedientthat
the powers forthe supply of electricityconferredby the
saidAct should be repealedin respectof the Company's
area of supply.
And whereas itisexpedientthat the other powers
mentioned in thisAct be conferredon the Company and
that such otherprovisionsbe made as are in thisAct
contained .
A.D. 1928 .

situationsand levelsof the severalworks authorisedby

to be taken or used for the purposes of thisAct with a
book ofreferencecontainingthe names ofthe owners and
lesseesor reputed owners and lesseesand of the occupiers
ofthoselandsand propertyhave been depositedwith the
Clerks of the Peace for the counties of Antrim and

as the depositedplans sectionsand book of reference.
And whereas the purposes of thisAct cannot be
effectedwithout the authorityof Parliament :

That itmay be enacted AND BE IT ENACTED by the

PART I. PRELIMINARY .
1. This Act may be citedas the Antrim Electricity
Supply Act (Northern Ireland), 1928.
2. This Act isdivided into parts as follows:-
Part I.- Preliminary .
Part II.- Incorporation of Company ,
Capitaletc.
Part III.- Administrative provisions.
Part IV.- Works , Lands , etc.Part V.- Supply of Electricity.
Part VI . Protective Provisions .
Part VII.- Miscellaneous .

Company or theirundertaking.

PART VI . PROTECTIVE PROVISIONS .
96.-( 1) Any electricitysuppliedunder thisAct to
any company body or person shallnot be used by the
company body or personreceivingsuch supply in such
manner astocauseor be likelytocauseany interference
(whether by inductionor otherwise)with any telegraphic
line(as definedby the Telegraph Act 1878) belongingto
or used by the Postmaster-General or with telegraphic
communication by means of such line. But thispro-
visionshallnot apply to any such company body or
person who are or isauthorisedto use electricityby Act
of Parliament or by an Order confirmedby or having the
effectof an Act of Parliament containingprovisionsfor
the protectionof the telegraphiclinesof the Postmaster-
General againstthe use of electricity.
(2) Sectionfourteenof the Schedule to the Act of
1899 so far as it relates to the Postmaster -General shall
apply tothe constructionor layingdown under thisAct of
any works across or along any land railway canal or
navigationwhether below orabove ground inlikemanner
as itappliesto the executionof works inunder along or
acrossany streetor public bridge.
(3) Nothing in thisAct shallprejudiceor affect
the rightsof the Postmaster-General in relationto rail
